## Contexts in which the phrase **soviet union** was used in the Senate during the 1970s

* Has the Australian Government been consulted about the offer of the base to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700317_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-10-0)

* Did the Prime Minister state in the House of Representatives in September and October last that the Government would not favour the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>'s obtaining base facilities in the Indian Ocean area? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700317_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-10-0)

* Did the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> veto a proposal in 1951 and 1957 that South Vietnam be admitted to the United Nations, a proposal supported by all other members  of the Security Council? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700317_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-7-0)

* Finally, is it a fact that in 1957 the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> proposed that South Vietnam and North Vietnam- [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700317_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-7-0)

* Is it a fact that no Tasmanian meat was included in the last Australian shipment of meat to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700617_senate_27_s44/#subdebate-6-0)

* Does the Minister subscribe to the views expressed by  Senator Wright  when representing the Minister for Foreign Affairs in the former Government, that any fragmentation of Yugoslavia as desired by certain members of the Croation Liberation Movement would increase tension in Europe and provide an opportunity for the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> to pursue its expansionist territorial policy? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-4-0)

* 
 - Senator Hannan has requested that the Prime Minister  (Mr Whitlam)  take certain action in regard to the statements that have been made about the events in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730912_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-41-0)

* That this Senate recognising that the question of human rights is a matter of universal significance, believes there is prima facie' evidence to support allegations by Alexander Solzhenitsyn and Andrei Sakharov that human rights of political dissidents are being abrogated inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and resolves that this question should be referred to the Human Rights Committee of the United Nations for examination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730918_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-2-2)

* (Quorum formed) I was saying that at a meeting of the Australian Labor Party some 1 8 months or 2 years ago it was resolved that there should be forwarded to the international socialist parties throughout the world the text of a resolution passed at our meeting deploring attacks by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> on some sections of the Jewish fraternity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I thank all honourable senators on both sides of the chamber for the spirit in which they have entered into the debate and indicated their support for the motion on human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* 1 ) that they oppose the Australian Government's recognition of the incorporation of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-0)

* 3 ) that the Government should appreciate that the Baltic States were unlawfully occupied in 1940 by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> through using armed forces following the signing of a pact by Stalin and Hitler. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-0)

* The question of advising the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> did not come into it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-18-0)

* Is the Minister for Foreign Affairs aware that on 4 August the Leader of the Opposition,  Mr Snedden,  posed a series of questions to the Prime Minister relating to reports that Australia had recognised the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>'s jurisdiction over the Baltic states? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-18-0)

* Will the Minister say when the Government of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> was informed of the Australian Government's change of policy? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-18-0)

* I refer to the situation concerning the Government's recognition of the Baltic states as part of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-13-0)

* Has Australia decided to grant de jure recognition to the incorporation of the independent states of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-9-0)

* That the Australian Government's willingness to officially recognise the incorporation of the Baltic States into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> will cause considerable difficulties to former citizens of Baltic countries who have acquired Australian citizenship and are revisiting the countries of their origin. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-2)

* By this hasty act, taken without consultation with the groups of Australian citizens concerned, the Australian Government has seemingly recognised the Soviet claim that the Baltic immigrants, upon their arrival in Australia, were really citizens of the U.S.S.R., and as such are not entitled to assume the protection of Australian citizenship until released from the citizenship of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-2)

* The Russian author, Alexander Solzhenitsyn, has revealed the detail's of the crimes against tens of millions of people in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> through the activities of the secret police and vast concentration camps. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-1)

* The humble petition of the citizens of Australia respectfully sheweth that: the decision to recognize the incorporation of the Baltic countries- Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania- into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is an alarming and dangerous reversal of foreign policy by the Australian Government, this decision legitimizes the occupation of formerly free and independent nations by an imperialist power, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has suppressed civil liberties in the Baltic states and has tried to ruthlessly eliminate movements for national identity and self-determination among the Baltic people, the desires of the Baltic people have always been and will continue to be for an end to occupation by a foreign power and a return to self-determination of government, there are neither moral nor legal grounds for legitimizing the present regime in the Baltic countries, all other democratic nations have refused to recognize the illegal incorporation of these countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-0)

* Your petitioners therefore humbly pray that the Australian Government rescind its decision to acknowledge the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> as the rightful government of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania, and support the continuing struggle of the Baltic people for national liberation and self-determination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-0)

* And the Senate requests that the Australian Government revokes its de jure recognition of the incorporation of the Baltic states of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-0)

* Whereas the six million people of the Baltic States of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania, occupied and unlawfully annexed by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, have been deprived of freedom. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-6)

* That the Australian Government's diplomatic action to recognise officially the incorporation of the Baltic States into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has been taken contrary to the Prime Minister's assurances to Australian citizens of Baltic origin given as recently as 1 7 May 1974. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-5)

* The undersigned citizens of Australia of Baltic origin wish to express their concern at the announced intention of the Australian Government to recognize the annexation of the three Baltic States of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-4)

* The undersigned citizens of Australia of Baltic origin wish to express their concern at the announced intention of the Australian Government to recognize the annexation of the three Baltic States of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-3)

* Whereas the Governments of the United Kingdom, the United States of America, Canada and many European countries have not recognized the unlawful annexation of the Baltic States of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, it has been announced from Moscow that the Australian Government is now recognizing them as part of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740815_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-4)

* Can the Minister for Foreign Affairs provide any details of the condition of the Australian tourists who were injured in a bus smash in Kiyev in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740816_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-8-0)

* The humble petition of the undersigned citizens of the Commonwealth respectfully showeth: whereas the Government of the United Kingdom, United States of America, Canada and many European countries have not recognised the unlawful annexation of the Baltic States- Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the Prime Minister of [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740919_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-2)

* The humble petition of the undersigned citizens of the Commonwealth respectfully showeth: whereas the Government of the United Kingdom, United States of America, Canada and many European countries have not recognised the unlawful annexation of the Baltic States- Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the Prime Minister of Australia has authorised the de jure recognition of this annexation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740919_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-1)

* The humble petition of the undersigned citizens of the Commonwealth respectfully showeth: whereas the Government of the United Kingdom, United Stales of America, Canada and many European countries have not recognised the unlawful annexation of the Baltic States- Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the Prime Minister of Australia has authorised the de jure recognition of this annexation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740919_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-0)

* Whilst the Australian Government is granting freedom and independence to Papua and New Guinea, the once free Baltic States of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania are occupied by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and their citizens are continuously and brutally deprived of personal, civil and religious freedoms. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740919_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-3)

* Did  Mr Bukevicius  specifically ask if  Mr Whitlam,  as head of the Australian Government, was going 'to continue not to recognise the incorporation of the Baltic States into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> or should we expect a policy change on this matter'. * If no bans have been placed on trade or other communications with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> or Cuba, is this another example of the double standard of left wing groups who attack so-called expansive aggressive acts by right wing governments but are noticeably silent in relation to aggressive acts by communist governments? * He further informs me that  President  Carter's reference to the proposed demilitarisation of the Indian Ocean was made when he was detailing arms control proposals which the United States has put to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. * As honourable senators will know, members of the new United States Administration have said in testimony before the Congress that the Administration would be interested in negotiating with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> on arms limitation in the Indian Ocean. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770310_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-3-0)

* I intend to speak very briefly but would like to congratulate  Senator Wheeldon,  the  Chairman  of the Sub-Committee on Human Rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> upon the tremendous work that he has done in producing this report, also the members of his committee including, from this chamber,  Senator Sibraa, Senator Martin,  and  Senator Scott,  who was originally also a member. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* As  Senator Wheeldon  has said, the Committee's first reference was the situation of the Jews in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and later that reference was widened. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The report deals at great length with the situation of people of the Jewish faith and persuasion in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Like  Senator Wheeldon,  I would not be worried if the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> wanted to inquire into a section of the Australian public. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Attaches weight to the statements by the governments of the United States, United Kingdom and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> declaring their intention to seek immediate Security Council action to provide help to any nonnuclear weapons State party to the treaty that is subject to aggression or the threat of aggression with nuclear weapons. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700304_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-43-0)

* The point I am making on the sophisticated approach is that the United States and Britain, if they can do so at any time, skilfully play off China against the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in world politics. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700304_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-61-0)

* If we were to capitalise on any schism between the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and China, that would be well and good. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700304_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-61-0)

* But some people in the Department of External Affairs have said thai Australia ought to rely on the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700304_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-61-0)

* Probably all members of Parliament have received all sorts of representations from some people who are antagonistic to almost every Eastern European Government, even to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700305_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-38-0)

* The Communist system has in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the Communist Republic of China and North Vietnam slaughtered more of its own people than were killed in two world wars. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700311_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-36-0)

* In September 1952 the Republic of South Vietnam was denied admission to the United Nations by one vote - the veto of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700312_senate_27_s43/#debate-39)

* However, with the veto of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, South Vietnam was denied formal recognition. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700312_senate_27_s43/#debate-39)

* Mr B.  Gafurov of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700407_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-4-0)

* Only in today's newspapers I noted that the Ford company had been offered a big sum to build a motor lorry factory in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700422_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-37-0)

* Only 3 or 4 years ago the Fiat motor company in Italy won a contract to build a motor car factory in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700422_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-37-0)

* The contract is to build this factory in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, because the Soviet Government simply was not supplying its own people with motor cars. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700422_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-37-0)

* The Fiat company won the contract to build this factory in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and to operate it, because the Soviet had shown itself to be incapable of providing motor cars for its own people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700422_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-37-0)

* In that and in other respects the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> certainly has not delivered the goods to its own people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700422_senate_27_s43/#subdebate-37-0)

* Although the Republic's admission was vetoed by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in the Security Council, the USSR had itself put forward in the General Assembly in January 1967, a draft resolution for the simultaneous admission of both North and South Vietnam, arguing that, as in Korea, two separate States existed with different political and economic structures. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700603_senate_27_s44/#subdebate-35-0)

* I am sure that he would not find it amusing if he heard about something like this happening in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, for example. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700616_senate_27_s44/#subdebate-66-0)

* In view of the encouragement and support given by some members of the Victorian branch of the Australian Labor Party to the North Vietnamese, Vietcong and aggressive Communist imperialism, and acknowledging that China and Romania have purchased rams and that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has expressed interest in purchasing rams, will the Minister draw the attention of trade unions to the fact that the ban is opposed to the principle of solidarity of Communist powers expressed by some members of the Australian Labor Party and sections of the Australian trade union movement? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700617_senate_27_s44/#subdebate-20-0)

* Although the Republic's admission was vetoed by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in the Security Council, the U.S.S.R. had itself put forward in the General Assembly in January 1957, a draft resolution for the simultaneous admission of both North and South Vietnam, arguing that, as in Korea, two separate States existed with different political and economic structures. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700819_senate_27_s45/#subdebate-44-0)

* Have executive members of a Jewish youth organisation recently made statements indicating that they would be boycotting the Bolshoi Ballet, currently touring Australia, because of the discrimination which exists in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> against Jewish people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700825_senate_27_s45/#subdebate-57-0)

* This has developed in place of the former bi-polar system involving the United States of America and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The balance between the United States, China, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and Japan- the quadrilateral in our region- is far from clear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Relations between Japan and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> are bedevilled by great differences over the return of the islands north of Japan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Only today it was reported that the Prime Minister of Japan,  Mr Tanaka,  left for a tour of Europe and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It was reported that he may reach agreement with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> over the return of the northern islands- this was disputed in other reports- in return for Japanese investment for the development of Siberia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* On the other hand, if Japan cannot reach agreement with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> will Japan reach agreement with China? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* There are reports- I think this was mentioned by  Senator McManus-  that there are between 44 and 49 Russian divisions along the border between China and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and that they are faced by an equivalent number of Chinese divisions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, obviously. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* No one who has any knowledge of military matters would say that the only threat would come on the border, that the only fighting would take place on the border, because everybody knows that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has nuclear submarines spread all over the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* If the Chinese feel that there is a threat from the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> then obviously they will try to match those particular bases and a situation could develop where the confrontation will be not on the border between Russia and China but in some remote part of the Pacific. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* That is why there have been negotiations between the Administration of the United States and the Government of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The dispute between the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and China is a black feature at the present time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 1 ) That this Senate, recognising that the question of human rights is a matter of universal significance, believes there is prima facie evidence to support allegations by Alexander Solzhenitsyn and Andrei Sakharov that human rights of political dissidents are being abrogated inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, and resolves that this question should be referred to the Human Rights Committee of the United Nations for examination; and [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Western rapprochement with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> could be dangerous if the West acquiesced over the lack of democracy in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, he said. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* He called upon the United States Congress to support the Jackson amendment which sought to place safeguards, in terms of liberty, in any negotiation between the United States and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* What we are saying- we are asking the Senate to support us- is: 'Please ask the Human Rights Committee of the United Nations to look into this matter because human freedom and human dignity in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> must be as precious to us as human freedom and human dignity in our own country '. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Just ask any Jew who has left the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> whether he was ever a hundred per cent sure that he would get out. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* The second technique is even more subtle: the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, by joining the Universal Copyright Convention (membership became effective on May 27), has ensured that works banned within the USSR can never be published abroad. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* The first is Andrei Amalrik, the internationally known historian whose crime was that he wrote a book entitled: Will the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> Survive until 1984'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* After all, at the present time we are in a particularly delicate situation in relation to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Whatever we think about the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and whatever we think about the United States, there is no doubt that the relationships between those 2 great powers will have a great deal to do with the sort of lives that we and our children will live in this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Whatever we may think of  President  Nixon, there is no doubt that over recent months negotiations designed to produce a real detente between the great rivals in the world- the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and the United Stateshave been in train. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Understandably, there is in the United States, as there is in the rest of the world, a justifiable concern with what I believe are clear-cut manifestations of repression of opinion by dissident intellectuals in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* On the one hand we have to strive to conduct our relations with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in such a way as to promote the detente. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* We have to face up to the fact that, whatever anybody may think about the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, it is not going to be puffed out of existence; it is here to stay for the foreseeable future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* We have to learn to live with it, just as the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has to face the fact that it has to learn to live with the capitalist United States. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I believe- I agree with  Senator Carrick  on this - that we do not do any service to the cause of detente or to the cause of liberty throughout the world by remaining silent about the repression which I believe is occurring in relation to dissidents in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Having said all that, 1 think we have to face the fact that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has come a long way since the days of Stalin when a Solzhenitsyn or a Sakharov, far from being able to trumpet an appeal to the world, would have been allowed nothing much more than to stand up in the dock and parrot a prepared confession prior to a quick death. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Nonetheless, I accept that in the terms of this motion there is a prima facie case to support the allegations made by the 2 leading Soviet dissidents, Alexander Solzhenitsyn and Andrei Sakharov, that human rights of political dissidents are being abrogated in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* The dissident movement in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> developed following Khrushchev's admission to the 20th Congress of the Communist Party that the horrors of the Stalinist period, which had long been known to discerning people throughout the rest of the world but which had been denied by the communist movement throughout the world, in fact had occurred. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* But members of what might be called the opposition in the sense of people who did not go along fully with the regime in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> were dissatisfied with the restrictions that continued to be placed on them even after Khrushchev's speech and some of them advocated radical changes to the social and economic system. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I think the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has reached the stage where it is no longer completely impervious to world opinion. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Among other things the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has reached a stage where it needs massive technical and capital assistance to develop its own resources. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I think that in a situation like this is behoves people in the rest of the world, like ourselves, who while accommodating to the fact that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> exists and is possibly a permanent fixture in world society, nonetheless to regard dissident intellectuals or human beings in general in those countries as people like ourselves, people in whose fate we have an interest and people for whom we are prepared to raise our voices. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Whilst I disagree with  Senator Hannan  on many of his views of the world, especially his view of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, I applaud his raising of this issue. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I would hope, as I said when I got to my feet, that everybody who speaks in this debate will speak responsibly, will speak without hate and will speak with a knowledge that we can no longer afford the luxury of just sounding off about what we do not like in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> or, if it comes to that, what we do not like in the United States. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* But I think it behoves any people who claim to be civil libertarians and who claim to be democrats to raise their voices against the sort of repression which I am convinced is occurring in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> at present. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* So I feel no inhibition whatsoever although I belong to a Party which has traditionally been considered to be over-partial to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Whilst not resiling from the proposition that we should restrain ourselves from any violent attack on the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, I feel no inhibitions at all in solidarising with the speakers who suggested and who moved that we should speak up on behalf of Solzhenitsyn, Sakharov, Amalrik, Grigorenko and all those other courageous dissidents in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Honourable senators would know that since he has become Chancellor he has devoted a lot of his energies to a detente with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I wasn't proposing, and despite your invitation I don't think it's likely that I will, to protest to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> about these matters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* But I quoted this extract as an illustration of the fact that our own Prime Minister is not unconscious of what is happening in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in respect of dissident intellectuals and that he also solidarises himself with their cause. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Australia- this present Government- believes, together with other Western countries, that this detente is in the interests not only of the people of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> but also of the people of the world at large. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* If we are sincere- and I give credit to the mover and seconder of the motion as being sincere- in our attempt to help these men I believe that we can do so by being restrained, temperate, avoiding hymns of hate and by reminding the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> that it lives in the world, that it needs the goodwill and the help of the world to develop its own system to nourish in the world and that the cause of detente is served by paying regard to the liberties which are considered to be a minimum requirement of civilised society. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I also was pleased to note what  Senator James  McClelland said about the situation in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, as he sees it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* But protest had this impact within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> only when it was backed 'by the united, mighty voice of hundreds of prominent people, by the opinions of a whole continent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* The importance of this motion arises from these developments which seem to have occurred in recent years in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* That is the tendency which now seems to be growing in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> to confine dissidents to psychiatric hospitals. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Of course, we all know that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is not the only country in which there are infringements of human rights. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Scientists and writers throughout the world have been assailing the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>'s handling of dissident intellectuals. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* I don't think it's likely that I will protest to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> about these matters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Why is not the Australian Government prepared to protest to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Why is it not prepared to take this stand with regard to the protection of individuals in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* We know that at present there is a growing detente and a so-called closer relationship between the governments of the Western world, in particular the United States, and the Government of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. * Yet, whilst the United States of America is stating these things as objectives of detente- of this closer relationship- as it seems the position in terms of growing contacts with Russia at the same time we are finding a clamping down in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> of any movement for freer contact, freer information and the interchange of it amongst the Soviet intellectuals. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* But surely if that obligation is recognised by this Government, why is it not an obligation which is also maintained and exercised in relation to what is now happening in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* After the words '<span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>', insert 'and other countries throughout the world '. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* 1 ) That this Senate, recognising that the question of human rights is a matter of universal significance, believes there is evidence to support allegations that human rights of political dissidents are being abrogated inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and other countries throughout the world, and resolves that this question should be referred to the Human Rights Committee of the United Nations for examination; and [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-66-0)

* Tonight we had broad unanimity in relation to the question of oppression in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-76-0)

* It is this: The Arab attack could not have been launched had it not been for the military and political support of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>- support about which the Arabs and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> have made no secret. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* It has been not only a matter of Moscow building for the Arab States a massive arsenal of its most advanced weapons but it has been the urging and goading of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> which has allowed and enabled the Arabs to feel confident in their military planning. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* The United States and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> have a special responsibility to do everything in their power so that conflicts on situations will not arise which would increase international tension. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* Yakob Malik, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> 's Ambassador, not only supported the military activities of Egypt and Syria against Israel, but criticised the Security Council for even raising the question at the United Nations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* Meanwhile, and this is the main point, the information coming to the United Nations was that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> while committed to reduce tension under the Nixon-Brezhnev agreement was actually urging Algeria, Lebanon and particularly the King of Jordan to get into the war against Israel. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* In conclusion, let me say that today we hear authoritative reports that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is re-supplying heavy weapons to the Egyptians and the Syrians and that the war is to be a long and bitter one. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* After all, only the other night the Senate unanimously passed a resolution to go to the United Nations on the question of the dissident intellectuals in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731011_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-39-0)

* In the making of its attitude known to the Soviet Government, did the Australian Government specify restrictions on Jewish immigration from the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> as an instance of denial of this fundamental human right? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731016_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-27-0)

* Did the Australian Government protest, that is, did it make a formal statement of dissent or disapproval, to the Soviet Government specifically concerning that Government's refusal to allow free immigration of Jewish citizens of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731016_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-27-0)

* However, in view of the fact that the war has now proceeded to the stage where the United States and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> are supplying large quantities of arms to both sides, I ask whether it is not time that the Government should use its undoubted influence at the United Nations level and internationally to promote a ceasefire. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-12-0)

* This was illustrated by the very large purchase recently by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> of 200,000 tons of butter from the European Economic Community countries at the give-away price of 22c per lb. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731024_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-14-0)

* In view of these lying statements put out by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in regard to the cause of the conflict, and in view of the fact that a tiny nation of 3 million people is confronted by the Arab nations of 1 10 million people, backed by one of the world's super powers, can the Government still adhere to its declaration of neutrality? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731024_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-24-0)

* I note that both the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and the United States were criticised together for the supply of arms. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* I do not accept that a even handed policy blames the United States to the same degree as it blames the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> for the war in the Middle East. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* We also believe- it is referred to in our foreshadowed amendment- that there must be an understanding and an agreement between the 2 major powers concerned, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and the United States of America, that they will ensure that there is no massive rearmament and that they will adopt an even handed policy on both sides to ensure that peace is maintained. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* Even if one were to argue that it was a mistake for the United Nations to decide some 25 years ago that Israel should be established as a state- even if one were to say that it should not have been done, despite the fact that the United States, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and practically every country in the world voted for the establishment of Israel- it is too late now to say that it was a mistake. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* Senator Little  would like us to make an heroic declaration in Canberra condemning, I take it, the Arab states, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and anybody else who happened to be connected with the Middle East position, and then to withdraw from the proceedings and take no further part in them, because that would be the consequence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* I would say at the same time that it seems to be quite absurd for the Senate to say that it is going to condemn the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> for selling or providing arms to the Arab countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* We can condemn the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> for providing arms to the Arab countries only if we condemn the United States for providing arms to Israel because there has been a two-sided traffic going on. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* It is not as if Israel is manufacturing its own arms and the Arab countries are getting their arms from the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* What has happened is that there has been a conflict of interest between the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and the United States with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> supporting certain Arab countries and the United States supporting Israel. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* I am not saying that either the United States or the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is acting maliciously or endeavouring to create havoc or harm. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731025_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-52-0)

* All we ask is that this young man be given the opportunity, free from intimidation and threats, to talk to those whom he originally trusted in order to make up his mind as to whether he wishes to remain in Australia or return to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. * If he declares that he wishes to return to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, there can be no argument- he has made a free decision. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-45-0)

* But if he returns to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, without this opportunity being given to him, in company with Professor Kabalevsky, this other character from the Russian Embassy and the others who go with him, no one will know whether he is going back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> of his own free will or whether he is going back under duress. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-45-0)

* I speak with an even-handed attitude because I have been equally vocal in relation to Polish seamen and I have even led a Yugoslav delegation to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, as  Senator Wheeldon  has done, complaining about its excesses. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-45-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-1)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-0-3)

* Is not this Professor Kabalevsky the same Professor Kabalevsky who was reported in the Soviet News Bulletin of September last year as having criticised Andrei Sakharov as acting contrary to the interests of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-6-0)

* In view of his attempt to equate the previous Government's decision in relation to Goa with the decision by the present Government to recognise the incorporation of the Baltic states into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, I ask him whether it is not a fact that Goa was a Portuguese colony populated by people largely of Indian ethnic origin whereas the Baltic states were formerly free and independent states possessing an ancient culture and traditions and whose people are witnessing the destruction of their culture and traditions and individually and collectively suffering from communist brutality and suppression? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-8-0)

* We notice, of course, that this is a right which the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> denies to its citizens. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* There are Valentyn Moroz and others who are imprisoned in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> because they exercised the right of free speech and the ability to dissent which we regard in this country as the right of every citizen and which we have always upheld. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* It is a shameful state of affairs, particularly when linked with the recognition of the Baltic states, that we should mould our foreign policy, decide issues of human rights and override the role of the courts in this country simply to curry favour with the Government of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Those circumstances are clouded by deception, stealth and, one can only suppose, an apparent sense of guilt and shame by a government which has no justification for its actions except that it gratuitously desires to curry favour with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* For 30 years this de facto situation has existed without any de jure acknowledgment of the rights of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in relation to these states. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The policy of the present Australian Government is that while not formally recognising the incorporation of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, it must be cognisant of the de facto situation and deal with the government which has effective control of the territory in question. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Is it because this Government desires to maintain with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> a relationship which it believes will be improved by the servile act of doing something which even the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> these days has not got on its shopping list of demands for other countries? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* We believe that what this Government has done has been done in order to facilitate a reception by the Prime Minister in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> when he visits that country this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Is not the only consistent view of the Government's decision to recognise the incorporation of these States the view that it accords entirely with the public attitudes of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* He persisted throughout the time that he was alive in assuring these people that Australia would never recognise the legal incorporation of these States into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* It may be an illusion to seek to maintain the ideal of freedom with regard to these countries because the de facto situation is certainly one in which the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has an all powerful control. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* But we have seen in the period in which the Labor Party has been in power a new subservience, and it is a subservience to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, to Communist China and to the nations of the Third World. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* What needs to be said is that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, because of the historical past, regards the 3 Baltic territories as just as much a part of its territory as Britain regards Scotland, Wales or Northern Ireland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I said that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> regards it in that way. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The week in which Ermolenko was spirited out of Australia and the week in which there was de jure recognition by Australia of the incorporation of the Baltic states into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> was indeed a shameful week. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The Australian Labor Party has not recognised and does not intend to recognise the incorporation of the Baltic states into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The policy of the present Australian Government is that, while not formally recognising the incorporation of Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, it must be cognisant of the de facto situation and deal with the Government which has effective control of the territory in question. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* It is opposed, as the Prime Minister himself has admitted, to the Universal Declaration of Human Rights which gives no support to the brutal annexation of the Baltic countries by the military forces of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The decision becomes more extraordinary when we are told and led to believe that there was no pressure from the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* In fact, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> was just as surprised as we were. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* But the Canadian Government has refused to recognise the incorporation of the Baltic states into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The Government itself, by its shameful act of recognising the incorporation of the Baltic States into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, puts its seal of approval, whether it likes it or not, in the eyes of the world, on this shameful, brutal Russian policy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* But if this Government were consistent, if it believed in the right of self-determination, if it really believed in the role of self-determination, then it would be giving aid to the liberation movements in the Baltic States so that they could overthrow the savage yoke of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I refer also to the Prime Minister's speech earlier when he made representations to both the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and the United States and said that the situation is hopeful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The next thing that was said, in a very colourful way, was that the Minister has prevented the courts of this country from determinng the issue of whether the young man wanted to go back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The courts were never asked to determine the issue of whether this young man wanted to go back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I find it very interesting that  Senator Greenwood,  who sent in the Commonwealth Police to arrest demonstrators at the Melbourne University, and who sent the Commonwealth Police to investigate and interrogate members of this Parliament for exercising this freedom of speech which he believes is so essential in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> but which at least in the past he did not think was of any value in this country, has today emerged as the champion of human rights, the champion of civil liberties and the man who says that a person should be able to get up and say what he likes whenever he wants to say it and that he should not be interrogated by the police, that he should be free to insert advertisements in newspapers and should be free to demonstrate at the Melbourne University or at the Perth airport or anywhere else. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Ermolenko said on a television station in Perth- he said it to journalists and to all sorts of people- that he wanted to leave Australia and go back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* He did leave Australia and he did go back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Their incorporation in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is one of the most shameful acts in modern European history. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* The argument is used- I think there is a certain amount of justification for it- that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> needed to take some steps to protect itself by entering into some sort of treaty with the nazis because the Western powers at that time had refused to co-operate with it and had rebuffed its efforts to organise a common front against the then menace of the Axis powers- nazi Germany and fascist Italy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I do not believe that this in any way justified the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> believing that it could forcibly incorporate those 3 states inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and I do not believe that it entitled the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> to occupy the eastern third of Poland and to take part conjointly with nazi Germany in a military attack upon Poland which was then, with whatever faults there may have been in the existing Polish Government, fighting alongside the democracies in defence of the world against nazism and fascism. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I do not think there is any question that the treatment of the ethnic minorities, the culture and the language of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania under the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is something of which the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> cannot at all be proud. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* What we are doing with regard to Lithuania, Latvia and Estonia is recognising an unpalatable fact of life; that is, that they have been incorporated within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and there is no foreseeable chance, beyond a third world war, of those 3 states coming out of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* We are not welcoming the fact that these countries have been incorporated in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* No, they are merely asking us to carry on with a farce or a fraud and to say to the people of the 3 states: 'De jure we do not recognise your incorporation inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, but de facto we do.' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* There has to be some recognition of the fact that whether we like it or not or anyone else likes it or not, or whether it is just or unjust- and I believe it is unjust and I do not like it- Latvia, Lithuania and Estonia have been incorporated into the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* To continue to say they are not part of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> while the Soviet Government and I daresay a majority of the Soviet people believe that they are is something which lessens opportunities for bringing about peaceful settlements with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, and peaceful settlements with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> are essential. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Today's variation to this theme goes something like this: The Prime Minister  (Mr Whitlam)  is contemplating a visit to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> at the end of this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Accordingly, for some strange reason which is not immediately apparent to me, it is therefore necessary for him to toady to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Despite everything that he had undergone in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, Solzhenitsyn still regarded it quite clearly as a severe punishment to be expelled from the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* Pasternak was a man who also suffered from the repressive regime of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* To suggest that anybody is in possession of evidence that he was kidnapped by the secret police and that our humane, tolerant, non-fanatical Minister for Foreign Affairs whose record will stand up to the epithets that I have attached to him was somehow acting as a stooge of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and went along with the idea of a kidnapping so that our Prime Minister would have a red carpet when he went to Moscow is in my view in the realm of spy fiction fantasy land. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* That, I say, is supported by the evidence of the conduct, behaviour and literary works of men who have suffered, as presumably he had not suffered, at the hands of the regime in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* I do not find it difficult to believe- as I said, I have no more positive evidence than honourable senators opposite have- and I do not find it at all incomprehensible that this man would have decided to go back to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> of his own free will. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740918_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-1-1)

* We believe that it is possible to have a just society without the oppression that has been practised in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and we are not heard to condone the tyranny that is practised in that country on individuals or in Russia's relationships with other countries. * For a long time we have been used to the fact that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has dominated in a quasi-colonial way a large number of countries in Eastern Europe. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* That was the case, but the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>'s influence did not go very far beyond that field. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* Despite the ideological differences which are supposed to exist between the policies of Colonel Gaddafi, a man held in reverence in some quarters, and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the fact remains that there are various very close relations between Colonel Gaddafi and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* The relationship which the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has been able to build up with various Arab countries has extended its influence into areas where only 10 years ago it had virtually no influence whatsoever. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* It has recognised that China is there, in the same way as the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is there, and that we have to deal with both of those countries as governments which have their own interests and set out to pursue their own interests. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* One can only hope that President Carter and his Administration will have the courage, the luck and the fortitude to carry through what they have said to be the objective of their Administration, that is, to pursue a policy in support of human rights wherever they may be throughout the world; that they will protest- and justifiably protest- about deprivation of civil liberties in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, in Czechoslovakia or Poland and will take action accordingly, provided it does not crash us into a third world war. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* This is exactly the same argument as was put by the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> at the time of its intervention in Hungary in 1956 and in Czechoslovakia in 1968 and which, as far as I understand, was rejected by honourable senators opposite. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)

* It was because the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> was supporting them and the western countries, which talk about democracy, were not supporting them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770322_senate_30_s72/#subdebate-40-0)
