* After some discussion the sub-committee came to the opinion that this was too narrow a frame of reference; that the question of human rights within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> went beyond the situation solely of the Jewish people although they did have particular problems. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> bearing in mind Australia 's support for the principles contained in the Universal Declaration of Human Rights and the Final Act of the Helsinki Agreement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Why is it that we should be looking at human rights within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, a country with which Australia has diplomatic and in many respects friendly relations? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* We believe it is important that the Australian Parliament and the Australian people should be informed on the situation of human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, for two major reasons. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The first is that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is a super power. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is much more important to know what is happening inside the United States of America and inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> than it is to know what is happening inside Bolivia or Uganda, or for that matter in Cambodia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* I am afraid I cannot say that of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* One cannot learn from listening to Radio Moscow what is the situation inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> with regard to human rights. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* That information can be obtained only by inquiries undertaken outside the official framework of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Apart from the importance of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> as a super power, the other reason why we believe it is important to understand what is happening inside that country is that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is an evangelical super power. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is the centre of a world-wide ideological system, a system which I would venture to say they describe, not entirely accurately- I do not want to get into a debate about that- as Marxism-Leninism. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has as its declared policy the extension of the MarxistLeninist form of government throughout the whole of the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Whatever they have not said, whatever they may have denied, whatever they may have been accused falsely of having said, there cannot be any doubt that, in any one of the major statements made by the Soviet Communist Party or the leaders of the Soviet State on any of their great occasions, they subscribe firmly to the view that the system of Government, the social system, the political system, the economic system, which applies in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is not only one which ought to be emulated elsewhere in the world but also is one which they propose to see is implemented throughout the rest of the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Indeed they have said, as  Mr Brezhnev  himself has said, I think on more than one occasion, that in those countries which are in close proximity to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, where there is a similar form of government- countries such as Czechoslovakia, Bulgaria, Poland and so on- the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has a right to see that they do not depart from that form of government, a doctrine which was not described by  Mr Brezhnev  in this way but which I think has been described accurately by others as the doctrine of limited sovereignty, the doctrine which justified the intervention by the Soviet armies into Hungary in 1956 and into Czechoslovakia in 1968. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The allegation has been made that this constitutes an interference in the internal affairs of another country, namely, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* proper that there should be an inquiry, whether it is regarded as interference in the internal affairs of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> or not. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* But one should not overlook the fact that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> itself is far from loath to comment on the internal affairs of other countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* But even the most enthusiastic and ardent admirer of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> would not be able to deny that any broadcast on Radio Moscow, any word or line that appears within any Soviet publication, appears only because it accords with the policy and the intentions of the Soviet Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* If an article appears in  Pravda,  which is the official organ of the communist party in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, that is an action by the Soviet Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has had a great deal to say about situations in a number of countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* I believe the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is entitled to do that. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* If it is free to comment on the situation in Northern Ireland and the situation in the United States and the situation in Australia and the situation in Chile, as I believe it is entitled, then we are entitled to comment on the situation inside the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* An additional reason why I believe it is important that we should be examining the situation with regard to human rights within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is a party to the Final Act of the Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe which was dealt with in Helsinki in 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> says that the Helsinki Accords are very important. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* I believe it is important that we should look at the record of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> with regard to the Helsinki Accords to see whether the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has been carrying out the provisions of those Accords in the conduct of its own government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* If it is quite proper for the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> to point to the superiority of the Marxist-Leninist form of government over other forms of government, I believe it is equally proper for those who subscribe to a democratic parliamentary form of government to just as persistently advocate the superiority of the democratic parliamentary form of government over other forms of government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* If the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is to say that its system is superior we are also entitled to say that our system is superior. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* If the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is entitled to point out imperfections in our system of government we are entitled to point out imperfections as we see them in its system of government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* They are of that opinion because the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and East Germany have taken the ideological struggle seriously. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* This is because East Germany and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> have persistently put forward the proposition that their system of government is better and they have set out to expose what they regard as weaknesses in the systems of other governments while we have not done the same thing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Imagine what would happen if we came down with a six page report saying that we had looked at the matter and that the situation of human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is unsatisfactory? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* -Before the suspension of the sitting of the Senate, I was dealing with some of the objections which were raised in the minority report of  Mr Armitage, Dr Blewett  and  Mr Scholes,  concerning the nature of the inquiry conducted by the Sub-Committee on Human Rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> of the Joint Committee of Foreign Affairs and Defence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Another objection raised was the difficulty the Sub-Committee experienced in obtaining evidence concerning the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* that Soviet Jews wishing to leave the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> had been consistently subjected to harassment and other forms of maltreatment and that their human rights had been denied, Soviet law and procedure infringed, and unwarranted punishments inflicted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Although during the last year there has been an increase in the number of Jews allowed to leave the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, this Second Colloquium  . [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* It should also be noted that the pattern of witnesses, which came before the inquiry, was partly due to the active participation of certain international groups, in conflict, with just cause, with the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Indeed, one can well wonder that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> would be trembling when it has the Latvian Evangelical Lutheran Church arraying all its might against the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and its allies! [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* I know that they have expressed opinions favourable to the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in and out of season. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* We are all familiar with people and organisations in Australia who have warm, friendly feelings about the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and who believe that it is a pack of lies to suggest that there is any infringement of human rights there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Not only did they not come from the Soviet Embassy; not one person, not one single, solitary soul, was prepared to come before the Sub-Committee and say one word of praise or commendation or excuse about the record of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> with regard to human rights. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is not that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is loath to provide information. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* I understand that when an inquiry into the presence of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in the Indian Ocean was conducted by a Senate committee the Soviet Embassy was happy to provide information to that committee. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* During the course of the evidence that the Committee heard from some people to whom I will refer in a moment, we learnt, I believe to my satisfaction- it would have been to the satisfaction of any reasonable person- that 300 dissidents are held quite improperly at any one time in Soviet psychiatric institutions, that their only psychiatric disorder is to be critical of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and that they include many eminent Soviet citizens. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* We learnt that contrary to the Helsinki Accords, to which the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is a party, there is not freedom of religion, there is not freedom of speech, there is not freedom of assembly and there is not freedom of migration, even when it is a case of the reuniting of families. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Among the witnesses from whom we heard was  Mr Leonid  Plyushch, a Soviet citizen, a man who was allowed to leave the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> as a result of pressure which was applied by the French Left, by the French trade unions, by the French Communist Party, and who still described himself as a Marxist. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is certainly the view of the Sub-Committee that whatever the virtues may be of inquiring into human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>- I believe it was probably more important than any other similar inquiry- we would be hypocrites if we were to inquire into human rights only in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and not in other countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-57-0)

* Senator Wheeldon  just made a magnificent speech denouncing the alienation of human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and Government senators were saying: 'Hear, hear'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* We have heard today from  Senator Wheeldon  about the report from the Joint Committee on Foreign Affairs and Defence on the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, which is obviously an excellent and most interesting report. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I suppose law in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> has a different meaning. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Minister for Foreign Affairs advises that the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> and governments in Eastern Europe, including Romania's, continue to deny fundamental civil and political rights to their citizens and that minorities often suffer most in this respect. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-35-0)

* It is amazing that on the very day that this Bill was introduced,  Senator Wheeldon,  on behalf of an Australian parliamentary committee, was able to criticise the breach of human rights within the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> which his committee, the Joint Committee on Foreign Affairs and Defence, concluded had occurred. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* It will be an interesting day when this is effective in communist countries, many of which have ratified the Covenant- the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, for instance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Among the countries that have ratified it are Bulgaria, Chile, Czechoslovakia, East Germany, Hungary, Iran, Poland and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Only a few days ago in this chamber we heard a report on the state of civil rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* A report on human rights in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> was brought in just recently. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Chapter 7 powers may only be exercised by the Security Council in which the great powers- the United States, the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, the United Kingdom, China and France- have a veto. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* We can have them in the socialist way, as people do in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> where the Government has given people the right to think their own thoughts, to meet, to work- all sorts of things. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* As  Senator Mason  said, the only one that we know of in the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> is reported to have blown up in the early 1960s. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791115_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-45-0)

* The Indo-China region is a major area of concern at the moment in that the situation may lead to further conflict between China and Vietnam and in turn may further involve the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in this area. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791120_senate_31_s83/#debate-59)

* There are a number of important issues mentioned in the report that I think the Senate ought to debate: The situation in Uganda today; the role of the Tanzanian army in Uganda; the elections that have just taken place in Kenya and in Nigeria; the role of the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span> in Africa; and the situation in Zimbabwe-Rhodesia today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791120_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-60-0)

* The activities of the fishing fleets of such major countries as Japan and the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, which previously exploited the ocean wherever and whenever they wanted to, virtually around the globe, have now been restricted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791121_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-55-0)

* Has the Australian Government concluded fishing agreements, within the 200 mile Australian limit, with: (a) Japan; (b) Taiwan; (c) South Korea; and (d) the <span class="highlight">Soviet Union</span>, and are agreements with any other countries being negotiated.
